<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">An ultrawideband miniaturized metamaterial absorber (MMA) in the ultrahigh-frequency (UHF) (0.3-3 GHz) range using a metallic incurved structure is proposed in this letter. Simulated results show that the bandwidth of the MMA with absorptivity more than 90% is 0.8-2.7 GHz with a relative bandwidth over 108%. The size of the unit cell is miniaturized to be only 20 × 20 mm<sup>2</sup>, about 0.0136 λ<sup>2</sup> at the center frequency of 1.75 GHz. Both simulated and experimental results show high absorption for TE and TM polarization over a certain range of incident angles. A simplified equivalent circuit and the current distribution for the MMA are presented to gain an insight into the mechanism to attain broadband absorption. On the aspect of application prospects, the MMA is promising as absorbing elements in UHF-RFID systems and 4G communications.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Since Landy <i>et al</i>. proposed a perfect metamaterial absorber (MA) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">
[1]</a>, there has been lots of research in designing an MA with good absorption properties such as multiband 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> and broadband absorption 
<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4 5 6 7 8" id="context_ref_4 ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8_1">[4]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>.
 Aside from research value, MAs designed in the ultrahigh-frequency (UHF) range <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10 11" id="context_ref_10 ref11_1">
[10]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_1">[12]</a> are also promising in engineering applications (such as
 UHF-RFID systems and 4G wireless communication) to prevent leakage of electromagnetic (EM) waves. However, limited to
 large cell size and narrow bandwidth in the UHF range, the MAs will be difficult to be used in practice applications.
 Thus, MAs with small size and broadband absorption are urgently necessary.</p><p>Periodic structures can be well miniaturized by using some bending shapes <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]
</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_1">[13]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_1">[14]</a> or using
 multilayer technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_1">[15]</a>. For the MA with narrow absorption band, increasing
 the number of resonance points <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>
, using multilayer structure <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>,
 and adding lumped elements <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>
 are all effective ways to broaden the absorption bandwidth. In these references, small cell size and wide absorption
 bandwidth generally could not be taken care of simultaneously. Besides, the use of a single method tends to have
 limited effect on improving the performance of MAs in the super high-frequency (SHF) range, let alone in the UHF
 range. Therefore, in consideration of these factors, MAs in the UHF range with both small size and broadband
 absorption are still challenging.</p><p>In this letter, a UHF-band miniaturized MA (MMA) with ultrawideband absorption has been designed and fabricated. The
 MMA unit cell is well miniaturized to be only 20 × 20 mm<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.144em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-4"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-5" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">^2</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> by using an incurved structure. Moreover, the MMA has a large absorption bandwidth from
 0.8 to 2.7 GHz, covering most of the UHF range with absorptivity more than 90%. Compared to other
 structures mentioned above, the MMA has only one closed loop, achieving ultrawideband absorption and high
 miniaturization degree simultaneously. Simulation results show that two key parameters related to the strength of
 mutual coupling between different parts can influence the positions of the absorption peaks. Then, a simplified
 equivalent circuit and the surface current distribution are combined to explain the EM coupling and broadband
 absorption. Finally, the experimental results are given to validate the good performance of the MMA.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Design and Simulations</h2></div><p>The front view of the basic unit cell of the proposed ultra-wideband MMA is presented in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(a)</a>, and the side view is presented in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1(b)</a>. The MMA consists of two metallic layers (the top layer and
 ground layer) separated by a dielectric substrate and an air layer. The top layer consists of a metallic incurved
 square loop loaded with lumped resistors. The dielectric substrate is modeled as FR4, whose relative permittivity 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-6" role="math" style="width: 0.964em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.505em 1000.84em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-7"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-11" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ε</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-12" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">r</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.803em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">{\varepsilon _r}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is 4.4 and tangent loss is
 0.02. The optimized geometry dimension parameters are given in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>
, and the resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-13" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.78em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-14"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-15" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">R</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the eight lumped
 resistors is optimized to be 68 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-16" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.66em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-17"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-18" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">\Omega </script></tex-math></inline-formula>.
 Notably, the size of the unit cell is miniaturized to be 20 × 20 mm<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX">
<span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-19" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-22"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-23" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">^2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, about 0.0136 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-24" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; <span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-31" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.144em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-32"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-33"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-34"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-35"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-36" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">{\lambda ^2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at the lowest frequency (0.8 GHz). The MMA is insensitive to the
 polarization of the incident wave because of its symmetric structure.

Since the background of the
 structure is completely copper laminated, the absorptivity can be calculated by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-38" role="math" style="width: 14.417em;  calculated result of the MMA's absorptivity is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>,

position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-111" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-112" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-113" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-114" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2.5</span><span class="mspace" id="MathJax-Span-115" style="height: 0.003em; vertical-align: 0.003em; width: 0.183em; display: inline-block; overflow: hidden;"></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-117"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-118"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-119"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-120" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">G</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-121" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">H</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-122" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">{f_3} = 2.5\,{\rm{ GHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, with absorption rates of
 96.30%, 98.21%, and 96.35%, respectively (result by HFSS).
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo2-2614703-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo2-2614703-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Simulated absorptivity of the MMA by HFSS and CST.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7580637/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The cell of the MMA is a compact structure based on a long incurved square loop. The total path of the current
 flowing through the incurved loop can influence the position of the lowest resonance point (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-123" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-127"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-129" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">{f_1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>). Then, the resistors stop the flow of current, thus the
 path is divided into several shorter paths, which can bring higher resonance points (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-130" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-134"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-136" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-12">{f_2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-137" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-138"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-139"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-143" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">{f_3}</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula>). Moreover, compactness of the structure can promote EM coupling between different parts,
 which may influence the positions of the absorption peaks, further facilitating a broad band united with several
 narrow bands.</p><p>Here, interval <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-144" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-145"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-146" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">e</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-147" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.14em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-148"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-149" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-150" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which may be two key parameters related to the mutual
 coupling <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_2">[16]</a> between different parts of the cell, are studied to examine
 their effects on absorption. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a> and (b) shows the absorptions with
 the size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-151" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-152"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-153" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">e</script></tex-math></inline-formula> changed from 0.4 to 0.8 mm
 and the size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-154" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.14em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-157" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> changed from 0.6 to
 0.4 mm, respectively. Further changing these two parameters will make the structure become extremely compact,
 which is also limited to fabrication technique. It is obviously seen from <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">
Fig. 3(a)</a> that the second absorption peak drifts to higher frequency, and the absorption rate drops to a
 value less than 90% around 1.25 GHz when changing parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-158" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-159"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-160" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">e</script>
</tex-math></inline-formula> from 0.4 to 0.8 mm. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a> shows that the
 absorption curves have a similar trend with the former curves when changing parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-161" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.14em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-164" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 0.6 to 0.4 mm. However, unlike the former curves, the
 third absorption peak drifts to lower frequency when changing parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX">
<span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-165" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.14em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-166"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-167" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-168" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 0.6 to 0.4 mm. The above absorption changes and frequency shifts can be ascribed
 to variation of current path when parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-169" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-170"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-171" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">e</script></tex-math></inline-formula>
 or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-172" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.14em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-173"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-174" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-175" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is changed. Detailed explanation of
 these phenomena will be shown in following parts combined with surface current distribution.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo3ab-2614703-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo3ab-2614703-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Simulated absorptivity of the MMA with the value of one parameter changed while the values of others
 unchanged. (a) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-176" role="math" style="width: 0.599em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.466em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.4em 2.384em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-177"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-178" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.754em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">e</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (b) <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-179" role="math" style="width: 1.524em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.194em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1001.13em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-180"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-181" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-182" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7580637/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The MMA is further studied under oblique angle of incidence for both TE and TM polarization as shown in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a>. For TE polarization as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">
Fig. 4(a)</a>, it can be seen that the absorption rate remains high over the range of 0.8–2.7 GHz
 with incident angle increasing from 0° to 60°. For TM polarization as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">
Fig. 4(b)</a>, the absorption curves have a similar trend with the curves for TE polarization. However, with
 incident angle increasing to 60°, the absorption property deteriorates sharply. The degradation degree of
 absorbing in TE and TM polarization for oblique incidence depends on amplitude of the incident components (electric
 component and magnetic component) to incident angle <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_2">[17]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo4ab-2614703-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo4ab-2614703-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Simulated absorptivity of the MMA at three incident angles for (a) TE and (b) TM polarization.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7580637/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo5-2614703-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo5-2614703-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Simplified equivalent circuit model of the MMA.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7580637/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The MMA can be seen as a simplified equivalent circuit shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>.
 Due to compactness of the structure, there will be a large number of coupling capacitances. For the sake of simplified
 analysis, the resonant modes at the frequencies <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-183" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; Thus, the
 resonant frequencies depend mainly on the equivalent inductance, which is related to the length of the current path.
 To further learn about the origin of three absorption peaks, surface current distribution is combined to illustrate as
 follows.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo6abc-2614703-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo6abc-2614703-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Surface current distributions on top surface of the MMA at three frequencies of absorption. (a)
 0.9 GHz. (b) 1.8 GHz. (c) 2.5 GHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7580637/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The current distribution on top surface of the MMA is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>.
 It is observed that the surface current presents obviously different distributions at different frequencies. Combined
 with the current distributions, we have divided the top surface into two zones (zone 1 and zone 2). It can be
 intuitive to find that the lengths of current path in zone 1 and zone 2 at the three resonant frequencies are
 approximately equal to their corresponding dielectric wavelengths (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX">

 _1}(or{\lambda _2},{\lambda _3})} {\sqrt {{\varepsilon _r}} }}} } {\sqrt {{\varepsilon _r}} }}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>= 159, 79, and 57 mm).</p><p>The resonant mode at the frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-376" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-377"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-378"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-379"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-380"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-381" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-382" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">{f_1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is
 caused by the current path both in zone 1 and zone 2, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(a)</a>
. By observing the animation of the current distribution, we also find that the current paths in zone 1 and zone 2 are
 changed synchronously, indicating a loose mutual EM coupling between zone 1 and zone 2 at this mode.</p><p>The resonant mode at the frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-383" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-384"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-385"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-386"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-387"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-388" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-389" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">{f_2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is
 mainly caused by the current path in zone 1 (at initial state), as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">
Fig. 6(b)</a>. When animating the current distribution, we find that the current paths in zone 1 and zone 2
 alternately decrease and increase (the total current path remains almost constant), indicating a strong mutual
 coupling at this mode. The benign coupling helps to extend the total current path in zone 1 and zone 2. Combined with 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>, when increasing the interval <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-390" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-391"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-392" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">e</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the mutual coupling will become loose, and then the current
 paths get shorter. Thus, the second absorption peak will shift to higher frequency.</p><p>The resonant mode at the frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-393" role="math" style="width: 1.024em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.9em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-394"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-395"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-396"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-397"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-398" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-399" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">{f_3}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is
 almost caused by the current path in zone 1, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(c)</a>.
 Combined with <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a>, when decreasing the width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-400" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.14em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-401"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-402" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-403" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">w2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the intervals between the incurved lines in zone 1
 increase. With the intervals larger than the interval <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-404" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-405"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-406" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">e</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">e</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the coupling between the lines becomes loose while the coupling between the two zones becomes tight.
 Thus, the current path will emerge at zone 2, and the current distribution will converge towards the distribution in 
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6(b)</a>. Due to the extension of the current path, the third absorption
 peak will shift to lower frequency.</p><p>Briefly, the second absorption peak is more like a bridge to link the first and third absorption peaks. It provides
 an idea for adjusting the positions of multiple resonate frequencies by utilizing coupling effect on current path to
 attain broadband absorption.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Experiment Results and Discussions</h2></div><p>The proposed MMA is fabricated with total dimension of 400 × 400 × 26.6 mm<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-407" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.144em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-408"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-409"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-410"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-411" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">^3</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (20 × 20 unit cells). <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">
Fig. 7</a> shows the MMA sample and the experimental environment, in which two log-periodic antennas and a
 vector network analyzer (Agilent N5230C over frequencies from 300 kHz to 20 GHz) are used. The MMA sample is
 fixed on a bracket in a microwave anechoic chamber. The transmitting and receiving antennas are placed on either front
 side of the center of the MMA sample to measure the reflection. The disparity of the reflection between the MMA sample
 and a copper plate with the same dimension can be seen as the absorptivity.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo7-2614703-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo7-2614703-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Photograph of the MMA sample and the experimental environment.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7580637/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> shows the measured absorption curves for TE and TM polarization,
 with the simulated curves given again for comparison. The experimental results show good agreement with the simulated
 results for TE and TM polarization at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-412" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-413"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-414" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">\theta </script></tex-math></inline-formula>
= 0°. However, the experimental results at <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-415" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-416"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-417" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">\theta </script></tex-math></inline-formula>= 30° are somewhat large in disagreement with the simulations, which is mainly caused by
 the direct transmitting/receiving (T/R) between the antennas because of their relatively wide beamwidth. The
 direct T/R will be more when increasing the incident angle. Furthermore, as the beamwidth of the log-periodic
 antennas in the H-plane is slightly wider than that in the E-plane, the direct T/R under TE mode can be more than
 that under TM mode. Hence, there are relatively larger errors in the measurement of absorption for TE polarization at 
<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-418" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.48em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-419"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-420" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">\theta </script></tex-math></inline-formula> = 30°. The measured errors
 may also be caused by some other factors, such as the inherent tolerances of the MMA sample in the fabrication process
 and the effect of edge diffraction of the MMA sample.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo8ab-2614703-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/7855842/7580637/zuo8ab-2614703-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Measured absorptivity of the MMA for (a) TE and (b) TM polarization.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/7580637/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, an ultrawideband miniaturized metamaterial absorber in the UHF range is studied. The cell size is
 reduced to only 20 × 20 mm<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="LaTeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-421" role="math" style="width: 0.483em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.144em 1000.42em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-422"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-423"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.423em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-424"></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-425" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">^2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> by
 using an incurved structure. Simulated results show a wide absorption band (0.8–2.7 GHz) with absorptivity
 more than 90%. By simulating the surface current distribution, we find the benign coupling from the compact
 structure can affect the shift of the absorption peaks to attain broadband absorption. Furthermore, experimental
 results also show a good absorption property within an incident angle of 30°. Moreover, such a design may have
 potential value as absorbing elements to be used in UHF-band applications.</p></div>
</div></div>

				<strong class="ng-binding">Author Keywords </strong>
				<div>
					<!-- ngRepeat: term in ::keyword.kwd track by $index --><span ng-repeat="term in ::keyword.kwd track by $index" class="ng-binding ng-scope">
						<a href="/search/searchresult.jsp?matchBoolean=true&amp;queryText=&quot;Index%20Terms&quot;:.QT.Miniaturized metamaterial absorber .LB.MMA.RB..QT.&amp;newsearch=true" ng-bind-html="::term" data-tealium_data="{&quot;keywordType&quot;: &quot;Author Keywords &quot;}" class="ng-binding">Miniaturized metamaterial absorber (MMA)</a>,

						<a href="/search/searchresult.jsp?matchBoolean=true&amp;queryText=&quot;Index%20Terms&quot;:.QT.ultrahigh-frequency .LB.UHF.RB..QT.&amp;newsearch=true" ng-bind-html="::term" data-tealium_data="{&quot;keywordType&quot;: &quot;Author Keywords &quot;}" class="ng-binding">ultrahigh-frequency (UHF)</a>,

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

Simulated results show that the bandwidth of the MMA with absorptivity more than 90% is 0.8-2.7 GHz with a relative bandwidth over 108%. The size of the unit cell is miniaturized to be only 20 &amp;#x00D7; 20 mm&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt;, about 0.0136 &amp;#x03BB;&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt; at the center frequency of 1.75 GHz. A simplified equivalent circuit and the current distribution for the MMA are presented to gain an insight into the mechanism to attain broadband absorption. On the aspect of application prospects, the MMA is promising as absorbing elements in UHF-RFID systems and 4G
